[12:0:164,553] 9800   Augmentation for Employee Compensation  

[13:0:66,574] This item reflects funding augmentations for state employee compensation. If the Legislature previously appropriated money,  

[13:1:66,584] through this budget item, to pay for the economic terms of employee compensation in previous fiscal years, the funding for  

[13:2:66,594] those economic terms is included in departments' budgets. When economic terms require funding not yet appropriated by the  

[13:3:66,603] Legislature, those funds are included in this budget item.  

[14:0:66,623] Additionally, this item sets aside funding for penalties the state may face under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Beginning in  

[14:1:66,633] 2015, the state became subject to the Employer Shared Responsibility provision of the ACA. This provision requires large  

[14:2:66,642] employers to offer health benefits to full-time employees, defined as those who work on average 130 or more hours per month  

[14:3:66,652] (or 30 hours per week), and their dependent children. Under this provision, the state may be subject to penalties (Part B  

[15:0:66,662] Penalty), which may include part-time, temporary, and seasonal employees that may have been considered full-time for one or  

[15:1:66,672] more months, were not offered or did not qualify for health benefits through the state, purchased health coverage from the  

[15:2:66,682] Health Insurance Marketplace (known as Covered California), and received a premium tax credit or cost sharing reduction.  

[16:0:66,701] The ACA also contains reporting requirements, which require the state to track specified ACA-related employee information on  

[16:1:66,711] a monthly basis to identify the employees who meet health eligibility requirements, document whether benefits were offered,  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — GG   164   GENERAL GOVERNMENT 

[1:0:168,69] 9885   Reserve for Liquidation of Encumbrances  

[2:0:66,90] For individual department budgets, encumbrances (commitments for the procurement of goods or services which have not yet  

[2:1:66,100] been received by the state) are accrued as expenditures by departments at year-end and included in the expenditure totals.  

[2:2:66,109] This treatment is in accordance with the budgetary/legal basis of accounting and consistent with individual department budgets.  

[3:0:66,129] For the purpose of determining the overall General Fund balance, Government Code Section 13307 requires that  

[4:0:66,139] encumbrances should not be counted as a budgetary expenditure until the delivery of the goods and services. Furthermore,  

[4:1:66,148] Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) require that encumbrances be reflected as a reserve against the General  

[4:2:66,158] Fund balance and not as an expenditure, as in budgetary/legal basis accounting. Government Code Section 13306 and state  

[4:3:66,168] policy require compliance with GAAP whenever it is in the best interest of the state. This budget reflects a statewide adjustment  

[4:4:66,178] to reduce expenditures on a budgetary/legal basis by the encumbrance amounts to comply with Government Code Section  

[4:5:66,188] 13307 and GAAP. A reserve of fund balance for encumbrances for this same amount is shown in Summary Schedule 1 for the  

[4:6:66,197] General Fund.  

[5:0:66,217] COMPUTATION OF ENCUMBRANCE ADJUSTMENT  

[6:0:66,236] The State Controller's Office accumulated a General Fund encumbrance total of $5,272,100,000 from 2020-21 year-end  

[6:1:66,246] financial statements submitted by state departments. For budgeting purposes, encumbrances are estimated to be at the same  

[6:2:66,256] level for the following fiscal years and are assumed to be liquidated (paid) within the next fiscal year.   Upon completion of the  

[6:3:66,266] year-end financial reports by the State Controller's Office, the budget information will be updated in the spring.   The  

[6:4:66,275] Encumbrance Adjustment Table summarizes the methodology and the calculation for the encumbrance adjustment.  

[7:0:66,302] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[8:0:66,321] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY  

[9:0:66,340] Government Code Sections 13306 and 13307.  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:162,65] 9889   Public School System Stabilization Account  

[2:0:66,86] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, established the Public School System Stabilization Account (PSSSA) as  

[2:1:66,96] a ”rainy day“ reserve for K-14 schools.  

[3:0:66,113] Proposition 2 requires Proposition 98 General Fund deposits into or withdrawals from the fund each year, as well as two  

[3:1:66,123] preceding fiscal years, when specific criteria are met.   Calculation of a deposit or withdrawal from the   PSSSA does not change  

[3:2:66,133] the Proposition 98 minimum guarantee calculation.

[3:0:122,88] 9900   Statewide General Administrative Expenditures (Pro Rata)  

[4:0:66,109] Central service agencies, such as Department of Finance, the State Treasurer, the State Controller, and Legislature, provide  

[5:0:66,118] budgeting, banking, accounting, auditing, payroll, and other services to all state departments. The Pro Rata process apportions  

[5:1:66,128] the costs of providing central administrative services to all state departments and funding sources that benefit from the  

[6:0:66,138] services. Amounts apportioned to special funds for their fair share of central administrative services costs are transferred from  

[6:1:66,148] the special funds to the General Fund and the Central Service Cost Recovery Fund.  

[7:0:66,167] Prior to 2016-17, Pro Rata assessments to special funds were normally included in the appropriate departmental budgets. This  

[7:1:66,177] budget item included Pro Rata transfers directly assessed to special funds for those cases where appropriate funding was not  

[7:2:66,187] provided for in departmental budgets. Effective 2016-17, this budget item includes Pro Rata transfers assessed directly at the  

[7:3:66,197] fund level, rather than each individual appropriation, pursuant to Government Code section 11274.
